 ● Perfect! I've updated the phase plan with all 5 critical registry
   fixes. Here's what changed:

   Registry Hardening Updates

   Fix #1 - Filename Consolidation

     - Canonical: UNIFIED_SSOT_REGISTRY.json (all tools updated)
     - Deprecated: FILE_REGISTRY.json, FILE_REGISTRY_v2.json marked as
   aliases
     - Separate: ID_REGISTRY.json confirmed for doc_id counters only
     - Added: migrate-registry CLI command

   Fix #2 - Write Policy Enforcement

     - New component: write_policy_validator.py
     - Validates: tool_only, user_only, immutable, derived consistency
     - Mode: Fail-fast (strict), integrated into registry_updater

   Fix #3 - CAS Protection

     - Patch schema: Now requires registry_hash field
     - Validation: Compare-and-swap prevents lost updates
     - New test: test_cas_precondition.py

   Fix #4 - Schema Migration

     - Removed: allocated_at
     - Added: first_seen_utc, updated_utc (unified timestamps)
     - Updated: All components to use new fields

   Fix #7 - Fail-Fast Validation

     - Default: Strict mode (invalid writes rejected)
     - Prevents: Partial registry corruption
     - Test coverage: Write policy violations

   Phase Updates

   Phase 0: Added registry filename decision
   Phase 1: Added write policy spec, CAS protocol, schema migration
   Phase 3: Added unified timestamp validation
   Phase 5: Added write_policy_validator.py, CAS enforcement
   Phase 9: Added registry integrity validation gates

   Deferred to Phase 2

     - Edge/generator records (#6)
     - Automatic module validators (#5)
     - SQLite backend

   New Validation Gates

   22 gates total (was 16), including:

     - Registry filename test
     - Schema migration test
     - Write policy enforcement test
     - CAS precondition test
     - Registry integrity test

   The plan now guarantees SSOT integrity with no known correctness
   gaps.

 > determine if these recommened modifications should be made:According
    to your current registry + watcher documents (updated **2026-01-20
   to 2026-01-21**), the intended end-to-end loop is: **filesystem
   event → queued scan/describe → promotion patch → single-writer
   registry apply → derive/normalize → validate gates → downstream
   generators → notify**. The biggest automation gaps are where that
   loop is still manual, inconsistent, or not yet enforced.

   ---

   ## End-to-end process and where automation must be added/modified

   ### 1) Standardize the registry target (critical consistency fix)

   Your unified spec defines **one physical registry**:
   `UNIFIED_SSOT_REGISTRY.json` (or `.db`).
   But the runbook commands still operate on `ID_REGISTRY.json` in
   multiple places (validators/normalizer examples).

   **Automation change needed**

   * Make *every* watcher, validator, CLI, and promotion applier point
   to **UNIFIED_SSOT_REGISTRY.json** (or go all-in on SQLite).
   * Add a “legacy alias” shim only if you must, but do not allow
   dual-write.

   ---

   ### 2) Enforce “single writer” + promotion patches (registry writes
   must not be ad-hoc)

   Your automation descriptor flow explicitly includes:

   * **Stage 5**: apply promotions to the registry
   * **Stage 6**: validate after apply

   **Automation additions needed**

   * A centralized **Registry Writer service** (the only component
   allowed to mutate the registry).
   * Everything else emits **promotion patches** (append/update
   intents), never direct edits.

   ---

   ### 3) Make write-policy enforcement non-optional (tool-owned vs
   user-owned columns)

   You already defined per-column ownership/update rules
   (tool_only/user_only/both;
   immutable/recompute/manual_patch_only/etc.).
   Example: `module_id` is tool-only and recomputed, while
   `module_id_override` is user-only/manual patch only, with explicit
   precedence rules.

   **Automation additions needed**

   * Registry Writer must reject any patch that violates `writable_by`
   or `update_policy`.
   * The watcher/scan pipeline must automatically recompute all
   `recompute_on_scan` fields (size/mtime/hash/module_id/etc.).

   ---

   ### 4) Normalize on ingest, not as a separate “cleanup step”

   Your unified spec requires normalization rules like **`rel_type`
   MUST be uppercase** (and ingestion must `.upper()` it).
   The runbook treats normalization as a gate you run manually
   before/after changes.

   **Automation modifications needed**

   * Normalization runs automatically inside Registry Writer on every
   write (or inside derive/apply).
   * Keep the standalone normalizer only for audits or bulk repair.

   ---

   ### 5) Atomic apply + backup + rollback must be the default write
   path

   Your runbook already specifies the correct mechanism: `derive
   --apply` does **atomic write** (temp file + `os.replace` + fsync),
   creates a backup, and restores backup on failure.

   **Automation additions needed**

   * Registry Writer must always:

     1. stage changes,
     2. run derive/normalize,
     3. run validators,
     4. atomic write + backup,
     5. rollback automatically on any failed gate.

   ---

   ### 6) Watcher pipeline needs a real queue + coalescing + loop
   prevention

   Your watcher subsystem already describes key mechanics:

   * separate event intake from processing
   * debounce/coalesce bursts
   * “stability window” before acting
   * multi-stage flow (detect → analyze → act → record), with a clear
   emphasis on not thrashing

   **Automation additions needed**

   * Persistent queue (disk-backed), plus retry + dead-letter handling.
   * Loop prevention: ignore events caused by your own outputs
   (registry writes, generator outputs), otherwise you’ll self-trigger
   endlessly.

   ---

   ### 7) Generators must be driven by registry state (staleness
   detection + rebuild triggers)

   The unified registry schema includes generator tracking fields like
   `source_registry_hash`, `source_registry_scan_id`, `output_hash`,
   `last_build_utc` etc.

   **Automation additions needed**

   * After every registry update, compute a registry hash/scan_id and:

     * mark affected generators “stale”
     * enqueue generator jobs
     * on successful build, write back `last_build_utc`, `output_hash`,
    and the `source_registry_hash` used.

   ---

   ### 8) Validation gates should run automatically in two modes (fast
   vs strict)

   Your runbook has explicit “gate” thinking and optional strictness
   patterns (e.g., opt-in strict validators).

   **Automation additions needed**

   * Fast validation on every write (schema + referential integrity +
   policy compliance).
   * Strict validation on “publish points” (commit/push, release,
   nightly).

   ---

   ## Concrete “registry-related watcher events” worth implementing as
   plugins

   These are the high-value plugin events implied by your
   policy/spec/runbook:

   1. **FILE_ADDED / FILE_MODIFIED / FILE_MOVED / FILE_DELETED** →
   recompute scan fields + update entity rows (including tombstone
   handling). (Move/delete handling is currently the most likely
   missing end-to-end automation.)
   2. **WRITE_POLICY_VIOLATION_DETECTED** → reject patch + notify.
   3. **NORMALIZATION_REQUIRED** (e.g., rel_type casing, path
   separators) → auto-normalize or fail gate.
   4. **DERIVATION_DRIFT** (derived fields no longer match formulas) →
   run derive/apply.
   5. **VALIDATION_FAILED** → rollback to backup automatically.
   6. **GENERATOR_STALE / GENERATOR_BUILD_OK / GENERATOR_BUILD_FAILED**
    → rebuild pipeline + write generator status.

   ---

   ## The single biggest end-to-end issue

   Your documents describe the right mechanisms (single unified
   registry, write policy, atomic apply, staged pipeline), but they are
    not yet **wired into one mandatory automated path**. The work is
   mainly integration + enforcement:

   * **Unify registry target** (stop referencing `ID_REGISTRY.json`).
   * Make **Registry Writer** the choke point that enforces policy +
   derivations + validation + atomic commit every time.
   * Put the watcher on a **queued, coalesced pipeline** with loop
   prevention.

 ● Review Decision: YES - All 8 automation gaps must be addressed, with
   prioritization.

   These recommendations expose the gap between "well-designed on
   paper" and "wired up in code." Let me break down which are critical
   for Phase 1 vs deferrable.

   Critical for Phase 1 (Blocks Production)

   Must Fix Now

   #1 - Registry Target Standardization - Already addressed in previous
   update (UNIFIED_SSOT_REGISTRY.json)

   #2 - Single Writer + Promotion Patches - Architecture exists but
   needs explicit "Registry Writer service" component

   #3 - Write Policy Non-Optional - Already added
   (write_policy_validator.py) but needs enforcement in Registry Writer

   #5 - Atomic Apply Default - Already in design (temp-file-replace)
   but needs backup/rollback automation

   #6 - Watcher Queue + Loop Prevention - Already designed
   (work_queue.py, suppression_manager.py) but needs explicit
   coalescing + retry

   #8 - Validation Gates Auto-Run - Partially designed but needs
   fast/strict mode distinction

   Important for Phase 1 (Quality/Robustness)

   #4 - Normalize on Ingest - Should be automatic in Registry Writer,
   not manual step

   #7 - Generator Staleness - Deferred to Phase 2 (downstream
   generators exist but staleness tracking is not critical for file
   watching)

   Event Plugins for Phase 1

   The 6 suggested plugin events map perfectly to our existing
   handlers:

     - FILE_* events → Already in event_handlers.py (move/delete)
     - WRITE_POLICY_VIOLATION → Part of write_policy_validator.py
     - NORMALIZATION_REQUIRED → New, should be in Registry Writer
     - DERIVATION_DRIFT → New, reconciler should detect
     - VALIDATION_FAILED → New, needs rollback mechanism
     - GENERATOR_* → Deferred to Phase 2

   Recommended Updates to Plan

   Should I update the phase plan to:

     - Add explicit "Registry Writer Service" component (consolidates
   updater + validator + normalizer + backup/rollback)
     - Add normalization-on-write (not separate step)
     - Add backup/rollback automation to Phase 5
     - Add fast/strict validation modes to Phase 9
     - Document 4 new event types (WRITE_POLICY_VIOLATION,
   NORMALIZATION_REQUIRED, DERIVATION_DRIFT, VALIDATION_FAILED)
     - Defer generator staleness tracking to Phase 2 (document in
   out-of-scope)

   This makes the "single mandatory automated path" real instead of
   implied.

   Should I proceed with these updates?

 ● Perfect! I've updated the phase plan to close all 8 automation gaps.
   Here's what changed:

   Major Additions - End-to-End Automation

   1. Registry Writer Service (New Core Component)

   Consolidates: write_policy_validator + normalizer + backup_manager +
   registry_updater
   Pipeline: validate → normalize → backup → apply → verify
   Key Feature: Single mutation point - only component allowed to write
   registry

   2. Promotion Patch Interface (Enforced)

     - All registry updates go through patches (no ad-hoc edits)
     - Registry Writer Service enforces this interface
     - Reconciler and watcher both use patches

   3. Automatic Normalization (On Write)

   New Component: normalizer.py
   Rules: Uppercase rel_type, normalize path separators
   Integrated: Runs automatically in Registry Writer pipeline (not
   separate step)

   4. Automatic Backup/Rollback

   New Component: backup_manager.py
   Location: .dms/backups/registry/ with timestamps
   Behavior: Backup before mutation, automatic rollback on validation
   failure

   5. Fast/Strict Validation Modes

   Fast Mode: Every write (schema + referential + policy)
   Strict Mode: CI/release (comprehensive checks)
   Integrated: Registry Writer Service supports both

   6. Enhanced Work Queue

   Added: Retry logic with exponential backoff
   Added: Dead-letter queue for non-retryable failures

   7. Event Type Expansion

   Added 5 new event types:

     - WRITE_POLICY_VIOLATION (reject + log)
     - NORMALIZATION_REQUIRED (auto-normalize)
     - DERIVATION_DRIFT (recompute)
     - VALIDATION_FAILED (rollback)
     - FILE_ADDED/MODIFIED (already existed but now explicit)

   8. Generator Staleness (Deferred)

     - Explicitly documented as Phase 2 scope
     - Not blocking for file watching system

   Updated Artifacts

   New Components (3):

     - registry_writer_service.py (replaces registry_updater.py)
     - normalizer.py
     - backup_manager.py

   New Tests (3):

     - test_normalizer.py
     - test_backup_manager.py
     - test_registry_writer_service.py (replaces
   test_registry_updater.py)

   New Directory: .dms/backups/registry/

   New CLI Command: validate-registry (fast or strict on demand)

   Validation Gates: 30 Total (Was 22)

   Added tests for:

     - Single-writer enforcement
     - Promotion patch interface
     - Normalization on write
     - Automatic backup
     - Automatic rollback
     - Fast/strict validation modes
     - Event handlers (all 7 types)
     - Retry/dead-letter handling

   Key Decision Changes

   Added 7 new decisions:

     - Registry Writer Service as single mutation point
     - Promotion patch interface mandatory
     - Normalization on write (automatic)
     - Automatic backup/rollback
     - Fast/strict validation modes
     - Event-driven architecture
     - Generator staleness deferred

   The plan now implements the "single mandatory automated path" with
   Registry Writer Service as the enforcement choke point.

 > review this assesment and determine if accurate: According to a
   document from **2026-01-23**, the Phase Plan describes an end-to-end
    subsystem (watcher → queue → locks → ID allocation/rename → AST
   parse → descriptor artifact → promotion patch → single-writer
   registry mutation → reconciliation → CLI/runbook/tests).

   What you have **right now** (in the uploaded code) is **only a thin
   slice**: a standalone CLI that writes `*.automation_descriptor.json`
    plus an extractor that produces an “automation_file_descriptor”
   JSON structure. There is **no watcher, no queue, no locks, no
   registry writer, no promotion, no reconciliation, no config, no
   tests, no runbook**—i.e., most tasks in the plan are still
   missing/incomplete.

   ---

   ## Critical blockers (will prevent the plan from working end-to-end)

   1. **Importer wiring is currently brittle / likely broken**

      * `automation_descriptor_extractor.py` imports
   `python_ast_parser` directly.
      * The provided parser file is a **DOC-ID shim** named
   `DOC-SCRIPT-1272__python_ast_parser.py`, not `python_ast_parser.py`.
    It relies on `_docid_loader` and a target module path
   (`mapp_py.src.python_ast_parser_impl`).
      * Unless you actually have a real `python_ast_parser.py` module
   in the runtime PYTHONPATH (or you rename/package the shim
   accordingly), the extractor won’t run in the intended project
   layout.

   2. **Extractor output does not match the Phase Plan / Deliverables
   target artifacts**

      * Plan/spec require
   `.dms/artifacts/python_descriptor/{doc_id}.v1.json` and promotion
   into registry columns 81–100 (`py_*` fields).
      * Current CLI writes `<stem>.automation_descriptor.json` next to
   files (or an `--out` directory), not `.dms/...`, and it does not
   produce a promotion payload at all.
      * Current extractor skeleton is `record_kind:
   "automation_file_descriptor"` and uses `identity.file_id` (empty)
   rather than `doc_id`, and it does not emit the required `py_*`
   promotion fields or parse provenance (sha, parser_version, etc.).

   3. **Single-writer registry mutation architecture is entirely
   missing**

      * The spec is explicit: **Registry Writer Service is the only
   component allowed to write** the SSOT registry, enforcing policy +
   CAS precondition + backup/rollback.
      * None of the required modules exist in the uploaded codebase
   (writer, validator, normalizer, backup manager, patch logging).

   ---

   ## Task-by-task analysis (by plan phase)

   ### Phase 0 — Lock down scope + validate dependencies

   **Plan intent:** confirm integration points
   (UNIFIED_SSOT_REGISTRY.json, ID_REGISTRY.json, column dictionary,
   AST parser, CAS/write-policy rules).

   **Problems / missing work:**

   * **Registry naming + migration is not implemented.** Plan mandates
   UNIFIED_SSOT_REGISTRY.json as canonical and deprecating
   FILE_REGISTRY.json/FILE_REGISTRY_v2.json.
   * **Column dictionary update (81–100) is not implemented.** This is
   explicitly in DoD and deliverables spec.
   * **AST parser dependency not “validated”; wiring looks unresolved**
    (see blocker #1).

   ---

   ### Phase 1 — Architecture + file structure

   **Plan intent:** create the package layout under
   `repo_autoops/automation_descriptor/` and supporting
   config/docs/tests inventory.

   **Problems / missing work:**

   * **None of the required structure exists** (no
   `repo_autoops/automation_descriptor/` package, no config files, no
   tests tree, no docs tree).
   * **Naming mismatch already present:** plan/spec expects
   `descriptor_extractor.py`, but your current implementation file is
   `automation_descriptor_extractor.py`. That’s fixable, but right now
   it’s inconsistent with the spec’s deliverables inventory.

   ---

   ### Phase 2 — Work queue + locking infrastructure

   **Plan intent:** SQLite-backed UPSERT-by-path queue, stability
   gating, lock ordering, retry/dead-letter, loop prevention
   integration.

   **Problems / missing work:**

   * **No queue implementation exists.** Yet the plan requires a state
   machine and exponential backoff policy.
   * **Queue schema as written is internally questionable for
   “UPSERT-by-path”:** `UNIQUE(path, status)` does not truly dedupe “by
    path”; it allows duplicates across different statuses and
   complicates coalescing semantics (MOVE events especially).
   * **Lock ordering spec is incomplete:** plan says lock ordering
   “path → registry” while the event pipeline calls for locks on **path
    + doc_id + registry**. Without a single canonical order (e.g., path
    → doc → registry), deadlocks are easy.

   ---

   ### Phase 3 — ID allocation + file renaming

   **Plan intent:** allocate doc_id from ID_REGISTRY.json, rename file
   atomically to `docid_filename.py`, suppress self-induced events,
   registry row creation.

   **Problems / missing work:**

   * No `id_allocator.py`, no atomic mutation of ID_REGISTRY.json, no
   `file_renamer.py`, no collision logic, no suppression manager.
   * Current extractor/CLI workflow does not incorporate doc_id at all
   (no filename parsing, no doc_id assignment).

   ---

   ### Phase 4 — AST parsing + descriptor generation

   **Plan intent:** parse (no execution), extract
   imports/functions/classes/CLI detection, merge declared metadata,
   generate descriptor artifact, compute source sha, produce promotion
   payload for registry.

   **What exists:**

   * An AST-based extractor that merges “declared metadata” with
   inferred hints and returns `manual_fields_needed`.

   **Problems / incomplete wiring:**

   * **Wrong target schema:** it builds an “automation_file_descriptor”
    skeleton, not the Python descriptor artifact schema described in
   the deliverables (`PYTHON_FILE_DESCRIPTOR.yml` with
   provenance/structure/behavior sections, etc.).
   * **No promotion payload generation** (required to populate registry
    py_* columns).
   * **No hash/provenance fields** (required: source sha, parsed_utc,
   parser_id/version).
   * **Declared metadata contract is underspecified in the plan vs
   code.** The extractor claims `AUTOMATION_META` is authoritative, but
    the Phase Plan is about Python file descriptors and registry
   promotion; the “automation descriptor” concept is drifting away from
    the stated target pipeline.

   ---

   ### Phase 5 — Registry update + promotion logic

   **Plan intent:** Registry Writer Service (single writer),
   write-policy validator, normalizer, backup/rollback, patch logging,
   CAS `registry_hash` precondition, fast/strict validation.

   **Problems / missing work:**

   * **Entire phase is missing.** No `registry_writer_service.py`, no
   validator, no normalizer, no backup manager, no patch log directory
   behavior, no CAS checks, no schema validation mode separation.
   * **Without this, the core “deterministic SSOT” guarantee is not
   implemented** and the watcher subsystem cannot safely exist.

   ---

   ### Phase 6 — Reconciliation & drift repair

   **Plan intent:** periodic scan, detect missing rows/moves/stale
   hashes, enqueue repairs via work queue (dedupe), run full pipeline
   idempotently.

   **Problems / missing work:**

   * No reconciler, no scheduler, and (because Phase 2/5 are missing)
   there’s no foundation to enqueue/repair deterministically.

   ---

   ### Phase 7 — Validation gates (unit/integration/e2e)

   **Plan intent:** ~30 explicit tests including single-writer
   enforcement, CAS rejection, rollback, stability algorithm, queue
   coalescing, loop prevention, move/delete semantics, idempotency,
   reconciliation repair, dry-run safety rails, schema validation.

   **Problems / missing work:**

   * **No tests exist.** None of the validation gates are implemented,
   so “definition of done” is currently uncheckable in practice.

   ---

   ### Phase 8 — Packaging + runbook + CLI

   **Plan intent:** operational CLI with start-watcher (dry-run
   default, `--live` required), reconcile, describe-file,
   migrate-registry, validate-registry; plus runbook + migration guide
   + write policy doc.

   **What exists:**

   * A CLI that scans directories and emits
   `*.automation_descriptor.json` using
   `AutomationDescriptorExtractor`.

   **Problems / incomplete wiring:**

   * CLI does **not** implement any required operational commands
   (watcher, reconcile, migrate, validate, strict/fast modes).
   * Output naming/location does not match the runtime directory
   conventions (`.dms/...`) required by the deliverables spec.

   ---

   ## Internal plan/spec quality issues (problems in the documents
   themselves)

   * **Component numbering bug:** the Phase Plan lists “13. Registry
   Writer Service” and then again “13. Reconciler” (should be 14). This
    matters if you’re trying to map tasks mechanically or generate
   checklists from numbering.
   * **Deliverables inventory inconsistency:** spec says “Source Code
   (15 files)” but the tree shown includes more than 15 (watcher,
   queue, stability, lock, suppression, classifier, allocator, renamer,
    handlers, extractor, normalizer, backup, validator, writer,
   reconciler, scheduler, audit logger, cli). That’s at least 18 not
   counting `__init__.py`.
   * **Out-of-scope phrasing is confusing:** Phase Plan says “SQLite
   backend (JSON only for Phase 1)” while also requiring SQLite for the
    work queue; this only makes sense if “backend” refers to the
   registry storage format, but it should be clarified to avoid
   mis-implementation.

   ---

   ## Bottom line (what’s incomplete vs the plan)

   * You currently have **Phase 4-adjacent prototype logic** (AST
   extraction + a simple CLI), but it’s targeting an “automation
   descriptor” schema rather than the deliverables’ **Python descriptor
    + registry promotion** system.
   * **Phases 2, 3, 5, 6, 7, 8 are effectively unbuilt**, and Phase 0/1
    are not enforced in code or structure.
   * The plan’s “done” requires single-writer SSOT mutation with CAS +
   rollback + validation, and that entire spine is missing—so the
   system cannot be made safe by “adding a watcher” on top of the
   current scripts.

 ● Yes, there are additional critical problems not yet mentioned:

   Additional Problems Found

   4. Schema Confusion: Two Different Descriptor Systems

   Problem: There are two incompatible descriptor schemas in the
   codebase:

   A. AUTOMATION_FILE_DESCRIPTOR.yml (139 lines, current
   implementation):

     - record_kind: "automation_file_descriptor"
     - Purpose: Generic automation script description
     - Sections: identity, purpose, triggering, inputs, outputs,
   state_and_ssot, process, error_handling, observability,
   security_and_safety, compatibility, execution, testing,
   change_control, related
     - Target: ANY automation (PowerShell, Python, Bash, JS)

   B. PYTHON_FILE_DESCRIPTOR.yml (Phase Plan requirement):

     - record_kind: "python_descriptor" (implied)
     - Purpose: Python-specific AST parse results
     - Sections: identity, parse_provenance, structure, behavior
     - Target: ONLY Python files for registry promotion

   Impact:

     - Current extractor implements Schema A
     - Phase Plan requires Schema B
     - These serve different purposes and cannot be merged
     - The plan never explains how/if they coexist

   5. Registry File Chaos: Multiple Competing Files

   Found in id_16_digit/registry/:

     ID_REGISTRY.json                              # doc_id counter
     2026012201113004_FILE_REGISTRY_v2.json        # file entities
     2026012201111008_FILE_REGISTRY.json           # older file
   entities
     2026012014470001_unified_ssot_registry.schema.json  # schema only

   Problems:

     - Plan says "UNIFIED_SSOT_REGISTRY.json" should exist but it
   doesn't
     - Multiple FILE_REGISTRY versions exist (v1, v2)
     - No clear migration path implemented
     - Phase 0 requires "validate dependencies" but files are in
   inconsistent state

   6. Declarative Metadata Authority Conflict

   Found: REQUIRED DECLARATIVE METADATA (authoritative).py

     - Declares AUTOMATION_META as authoritative
     - Uses automation_file_descriptor schema
     - Has ssot_reads and ssot_writes tracking

   Conflict with Phase Plan:

     - Plan expects Python files to have minimal/no declared metadata
     - AST parsing should be primary source (inferred > declared)
     - "Declared metadata" concept not mentioned in Phase Plan
     - Extractor treats AUTOMATION_META as authoritative, which
   contradicts AST-first approach

   7. Multiple Parser Files Exist

   Found:

     - DOC-SCRIPT-0996__python_ast_parser.py (referenced in plan)
     - DOC-SCRIPT-1272__python_ast_parser.py (shim)
     - Both are doc-id prefixed, unclear which is canonical

   Problem: Phase 0 requires "validate AST parser dependency" but
   there's confusion about which file is the real parser.

   8. Test Files Exist But Disconnected

   Found:

     - DOC-TEST-0632__test_copilot_parser.py
     - DOC-TEST-0639__test_python_ast_parser.py

   Problem:

     - Plan requires 15 test files in tests/automation_descriptor/
     - These tests exist but are DOC-ID prefixed standalone files
     - Not in proper pytest package structure
     - Not covering the Phase Plan components (which don't exist yet)

   9. Config Files Missing But Referenced

   Phase Plan requires:

     - config/WATCHER_CONFIG.yml
     - config/PYTHON_FILE_DESCRIPTOR.yml

   Found:

     - AUTOMATION_FILE_DESCRIPTOR.yml (wrong schema)
     - No WATCHER_CONFIG.yml
     - No actual config/ directory structure

   10. Documentation Fragmentation

   Found multiple overlapping docs:

     - Automation Descriptor Subsystem.docx
     - ChatGPT-Automation Descriptor Subsystem.md
     - Automation_Descriptor_Phase_Plan.md (new)
     - Automation_Descriptor_Deliverables_Specification.md (new)
     - watcher subsystem.md

   Problem:

     - No clear "single source of truth" for the spec
     - DOCX and MD files may be out of sync
     - New phase plan doesn't reference older docs
     - Risk of implementation following wrong/outdated spec

   Summary of New Problems

   Critical Decision Required

   The fundamental issue: The codebase has implemented an "automation
   file descriptor" system (generic, multi-language, declaration-based)
   but the Phase Plan describes a "Python descriptor with registry
   promotion" system (Python-only, AST-first, SSOT integration).

   These are different systems. They need to either:

     - Coexist (automation descriptors + python descriptors, different
   purposes)
     - Converge (pick one, deprecate the other)
     - Adapter layer (automation descriptor wraps python descriptor)

   The Phase Plan doesn't address this, which means implementation will
   drift or conflict.

 ● Based on my analysis of the ChatGPT spec document, here are the
   critical missing parts from the Phase Plan:

   Major Gaps in Phase Plan vs ChatGPT Spec

   1. Dual Schema System Not Addressed ❌

   ChatGPT Spec Describes:

     - AUTOMATION_FILE_DESCRIPTOR.yml - Generic automation descriptor
   (all languages)
     - Purpose: "make every automation script self-describing"
     - Sections: identity, purpose, triggering, inputs, outputs,
   state_and_ssot, process, error_handling, etc.

   Phase Plan Describes:

     - PYTHON_FILE_DESCRIPTOR.yml - Python-specific AST results
     - Purpose: Python file parsing for registry promotion
     - Sections: identity, parse_provenance, structure, behavior

   Gap: Phase Plan never explains:

     - Do both schemas coexist?
     - Is automation descriptor for "special" scripts only?
     - How does declared AUTOMATION_META relate to AST-inferred data?
     - Which descriptor does the extractor generate?

   2. Declarative Metadata Authority Missing ❌

   ChatGPT Spec Requires:

     - REQUIRED DECLARATIVE METADATA (authoritative).py
     - AUTOMATION_META block is authoritative (human-provided)
     - Extractor merges declared + inferred, produces
   manual_fields_needed

   Phase Plan Assumes:

     - AST-first approach (no declared metadata mentioned)
     - Parser extracts everything automatically
     - No concept of "authoritative human-provided fields"

   Gap: Fundamental conflict about data source priority

   3. Process Contract (Formal Stages) Missing ❌

   ChatGPT Spec Provides (lines 769-949):

     process_contract:
       contract_id: PC_FILE_INGEST_ENRICH_V1
       stages:
         - S1_EVENT_INTAKE
         - S2_DEBOUNCE_STABILITY
         - S3_CLASSIFY_PLAN
         - S4_LOCK_ACQUIRE
         - S5_ID_AND_ROW_UPSERT
         - S6_ANALYZE_PYTHON
         - S7_APPLY_PROMOTIONS
         - S8_DERIVED_GENERATORS
         - S9_FINALIZE

   Phase Plan Has:

     - Vague stage descriptions
     - No formal contract definition
     - No machine-enforceable stage IDs

   Gap: ChatGPT spec is more precise about stage sequencing and
   contracts

   4. Registry Patch Schema Missing ❌

   ChatGPT Spec Provides (lines 953-998):

     {
       "patch_schema_id": "REGISTRY_PATCH_V1",
       "patch_kind": "file_row_update",
       "required": ["registry_version", "doc_id", "ops", "actor",
   "utc_ts", "work_item_id"],
       "constraints": [
         "All ops MUST target the file row identified by doc_id",
         "Patch application MUST be atomic: write-temp-then-replace"
       ]
     }

   Phase Plan Has:

     - Vague "promotion patch" concept
     - No schema definition
     - No op types (set/add/remove)
     - No constraint specification

   Gap: Phase Plan doesn't define patch structure

   5. Retry Rules Specification Missing ❌

   ChatGPT Spec Defines (lines 823-840):

     retry_rules:
       max_attempts: 8
       backoff_seconds: [5, 15, 45, 120, 300, 900, 1800, 3600]
       retryable_errors: [FILE_LOCKED, PERMISSION_DENIED_TRANSIENT,
   ...]
       non_retryable_errors: [POLICY_FORBIDDEN_PATH, ...]
       parse_errors:
         syntax_error_state: parse_failed
         repeated_parse_failures_to_quarantine: 10

   Phase Plan Has:

     - Vague "exponential backoff" mention
     - No specific backoff schedule
     - No error classification
     - No parse error policy

   6. File State Machine More Detailed in ChatGPT ❌

   ChatGPT Spec (lines 796-812):

     file_row_states:
       - discovered
       - registered
       - analyzing
       - enriched
       - parse_failed
       - quarantine
       - unmanaged
       - deleted
     work_item_states:
       - queued
       - stable_pending
       - stable_ready
       - running
       - done
       - retry_wait
       - dead_letter

   Phase Plan Has:

     - Only work_item states: queued → stable_pending → stable_ready →
   running → done/retry/dead_letter
     - No file_row_states defined

   7. Deterministic Artifact Formulas More Explicit ✅ (Mostly Aligned)

   ChatGPT Spec (lines 814-821):

     deterministic_artifact_formulas:
       python_descriptor:
         path:
   ".dms/artifacts/python_descriptor/{doc_id}.v{schema_version}.json"
       registry_patch:
         path:
   ".dms/patches/registry/{utc_ts}__{work_item_id}__{doc_id}.json"

   Phase Plan Has: Similar but less formal specification

   8. Python Promotion Columns Match ✅ (Aligned)

   ChatGPT Spec Defines (lines 1047-1175): Columns 81-100 Phase Plan
   Has: Same 20 columns (py_parse_status → py_descriptor_sha256)

   Status: ✅ This is consistent

   9. Reconciliation Requirements More Detailed ❌

   ChatGPT Spec (lines 754-765):

     - Discover missing files
     - Detect renamed/moved paths
     - Detect stale descriptors vs hash
     - Enforce policy/quarantine

   Phase Plan Has:

     - Vague "drift detection"
     - No specific detection algorithms

   10. File Inventory Specifications Different ⚠️

   ChatGPT Spec Lists (lines 591-645):

     - Canonical files (human-maintained)
     - Generated files (tool-owned)
     - Runtime files (ephemeral)
     - Clear separation

   Phase Plan Has:

     - File inventory in appendix
     - Less clear ownership rules

   Critical Missing Components

   Components in ChatGPT Spec NOT in Phase Plan:

     - descriptor_manual_fields_needed.py - Predecessor/alternate
   approach
     - Explicit "older/parallel implementation" retirement plan
     - Lock ordering specification: path → doc → registry (not just
   path → registry)
     - Stability check algorithm: Not just time-based, but mtime/size
   sampling
     - Quarantine directory structure:
   .dms/quarantine/{reason}/{doc_id_or_temp_id}/...
     - Patch log directory: .dms/patches/registry/ (Phase Plan mentions
    but not detailed)

   Recommendations

   High Priority (Breaks Implementation)

     - Resolve Schema Confusion: Decide if automation_descriptor and
   python_descriptor coexist or one replaces the other
     - Clarify Declarative Metadata: AST-first or
   declared-metadata-first?
     - Add Process Contract: Formalize stage IDs (S1-S9) with
   inputs/outputs
     - Define Patch Schema: Exact JSON structure for registry updates
     - Add Retry Rules: Specific backoff schedule and error
   classification

   Medium Priority (Improves Quality)

     - Add File Row States: Not just work item states
     - Specify Reconciliation Algorithms: How to detect each drift type
     - Define Lock Ordering: Three-level lock hierarchy (path → doc →
   registry)
     - Document Quarantine Policy: When/why files are quarantined

   Low Priority (Documentation)

     - Clarify File Ownership: Canonical vs generated vs runtime
     - Retirement Plan: What to do with
   descriptor_manual_fields_needed.py

   Summary

   The ChatGPT spec is more detailed than the Phase Plan in:

     - Process formalization (stage contracts, retry rules, state
   machines)
     - Patch schema definition
     - Error handling policy
     - Reconciliation specifics

   The Phase Plan is clearer on:

     - Implementation structure (repo_autoops/automation_descriptor/)
     - Test organization
     - Validation gates (30 specific tests)
     - CLI command specifications

   The critical gap: The two documents describe different systems
   (automation descriptor vs python descriptor) and this conflict must
   be resolved before implementation.
